    <li> About a year after I got my new Philips electric razor as a present I noticed it wasn&#x27;t shaving as close as it used to. Duh! The blades don&#x27;t stay sharp forever, dummy!     <li> My razor is an 8894 XL but others using the HQ8 cutters are similar. There is no reason not to replace the cutters when the razor advises to do so. It only takes about 5 minutes and most of that time is getting the package open. :)   When installing the cutters, lift them one at a time from the package and be careful to keep the 2 parts of each cutter together as they are matched.  To reset the \\&quot;replace advisor indicator\\&quot;, press and hold down the power button until the razor beeps. (About 4 seconds)  Then you&#x27;re good to go.  A new razor is over $200. Amazon&#x27;s price with free shipping is impossible to beat!</li>

At the time, lesser models came with NiCad batteries and held less charge and the higher model had lithium batteries and held more charge.    These heads keep my shaver going strong even after 6 or 7 years.  I get a decent shave without the mess of a wet shave with razor so I&#x27;m content.  Only problem I&#x27;ve had with my shaver are the batteries.    For the past year or so I noticed the run time on my shaver was decreasing.  It cost me about $8 to get two AA-sized NiMH batteries with solder tabs and about an hour to replace them.  My shaver is good for another 6 years unless something else breaks.  No reason to buy a new shaver if all it needs is batteries and heads to keep it going.  At $25/year I think this is less than I&#x27;d spend on blades.  Please note that not all shavers will use the same batteries; you&#x27;ll need to verify the quantity and size before proceeding with the replacement.  Replacement also involves cutting leads and soldering the batteries in place; it does require a bit of soldering knowledge.</li>

    <li> I got this set of replacement shaving / cutting heads recently, for my Phillips AquaTouch AT890 razor.  The razor gives a nice shave, and it includes a &amp;#34;replacement indicator&amp;#34; which lights up when the cutting heads need to be replaced.  Although the packaging says that the blades should be replace once a year the indicator only lit up after about 18 months, so I got extended use out of them.  The blades are relatively easy to replace.  I found the instructions on the package to be less clear than they could have been, but it didn&#x27;t take long to figure out - an assembly that holds the blades needs to be removed from the razor; small locking screws that hold the blades in place need to be removed; then the blades themselves need to be removed from the assembly.  The new blades need to be inserted into the assembly; new locking screws installed; and then the assembly placed back into the razor.  The replacement only needs to take a couple of minutes once you figure it out.  Shaving / cutting blades do need to be replaced, and Phillips has developed a relatively easy and effective replacement routine.</li>

    <li> My Norelco model has an internal system to let you know when to clean it, recharge it, or replace the heads based on actual usage.  Very civilized.  These replacements are very easy to install and do a fine job of restoring a close shave.  The blades and heads are matched sets and the blades are razor sharp (duh), so you need to be cautious not to let the head sets come apart, including when you open the packaging.  Each goes in only one way, so take note of where the flat spot on the side of each head is oriented as you remove each old head and match it as you put in the new.  I removed the heads and replaced each before moving to the next position, just to make that orientation easier.  This is much easier if you remove the entire head assembly from the body of the shaver first.</li>
    <li> Fitted my husbands needs perfectly.</li>

    <li> Like most users, after using an electric razor month after month, you just forget how old the blades really are. Sure they get rid of the stubble and ok, it may take a little longer with the passing months, but gee didn&#x27;t I just get new blades less than a year ago?  Usually it&#x27;s more like 2 years as in my case.  New head makes the shave lots easier and takes less time. Worth the $20+.  As for the guy that said his shave was worse with the new heads, perhaps he didn&#x27;t seat them properly.  The housing screen surrounding each rotary blade must seat fully. There 2 tiny angles that fit precisely into the housing.  Otherwise the blades can&#x27;t do their job properly.  I had that issue several years ago with a previous model although this one is engineered similarly.  Once I discover the issue, it hasn&#x27;t happened again.  Do it with good lighting and not first thing in the morning when your eyes haven&#x27;t adjusted to the world. Great razor.  My only caveat should you need a new razor and not just replacement heads, go with the model that is made in The Nederlands.  Avoid the Chinese, Mexican, etc models.  They cost a little more but are worth it for durability and longevity IMVHO.</li>
